## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population size P, which is the fundamental problem in population dynamics. Classical models range from simple exponential growth to density-dependent models like logistic growth, and can include time-dependent parameters for seasonal or environmental variation.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth rate decreasing logarithmically with population)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Strong Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (cubic dependence on P)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism vs catabolism scaling)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (flexible sigmoidal growth)
- Time-varying logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * t * P (logistic with time-dependent carrying capacity)
- Periodic forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal variation in growth rate)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (generalized density-dependent growth)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P / (P + c3) (logistic with saturating harvest)
- Exponential decay of growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (time-dependent intrinsic rate)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density dependence → Growth rate contains P multiplied by a factor that decreases with P (e.g., (1 - c*P) or log(c/P))
- Allee effects → Cubic polynomial in P, indicating negative growth at both very low and very high population sizes
- Carrying capacity → The term (1 - P/K) creates a zero-crossing of dP/dt at P=K, representing equilibrium
- Metabolic scaling → Different power-law exponents for growth and loss terms (e.g., P^(2/3) - P) reflecting surface-to-volume scaling
- Seasonal/periodic environmental forcing → Multiplicative sinusoidal modulation of the intrinsic growth rate parameter
- Depensation (inverse density dependence) → Growth rate per capita that increases with P at low densities, indicating cooperative effects
- Multiple equilibria → Polynomial expressions in P with multiple real roots indicate bistability or regime shifts
- Time-explicit environmental change → Additive or multiplicative terms in t reflecting gradual habitat change or resource depletion
